  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cd3bf16c-3281-48fd-a32e-f65e6c0fe4e6'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9867097674422123874">Tenk deg å mangle noe alle andre har. Noe som beviser at du hører til i denne verden. Noe så viktig at uten det, er du ingenting. En pest. En myte. Et menneske. <br/><br/>Femten vintre gammel får Hirka vite at hun er et odinsbarn - en halelaus råttenskap fra en annen verden. Foraktet. Fryktet. Og jaget. Hun aner ikke lenger hvem hun er, og noen vil drepe henne for at det skal forbli</span>
  <span id="freeText9867097674422123874" style="display:none">Tenk deg å mangle noe alle andre har. Noe som beviser at du hører til i denne verden. Noe så viktig at uten det, er du ingenting. En pest. En myte. Et menneske. <br /><br />Femten vintre gammel får Hirka vite at hun er et odinsbarn - en halelaus råttenskap fra en annen verden. Foraktet. Fryktet. Og jaget. Hun aner ikke lenger hvem hun er, og noen vil drepe henne for at det skal forbli en hemmelighet. Men det finnes verre ting enn odinsbarn, og Hirka er ikke den eneste skapningen som har brutt gjennom portene. Odinsbarn er original fantasy på norrøn grunn. Et oppgjør med fremmedfrykt, blind tro og retten eller viljen til å lede. Det er den første av tre bøker om Hirka, i serien Ravneringene.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hei, Oda! Dette spørsmålet har lurt seg under radaren. Har ikke sett det før nå, beklager så mye! Jo, jeg har møtt flere filmselskaper som har lyst ti<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hei, Oda! Dette spørsmålet har lurt seg under radaren. Har ikke sett det før nå, beklager så mye! Jo, jeg har møtt flere filmselskaper som har lyst til å lage filmene, og det er kjempegøy! Det handler om å finne de rette menneskene og premissene. Jeg håper og tror det vil skje, selv om det er et langt lerret å bleke. Tusen takk som spør :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788763842303" href="/book/show/29540966-odinsbarn">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1636017887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer577555361345773087">This is a YA fantasy story based on Norse Mythology. It was written by a Norwegian author, and so far it has only been published in Scandinavia, to my knowledge. <br/>That being said, I definitely recommend this book if you are able to get it and read it. It tells the story of Hirka who is very different from everyone else around her - that's because she has no tail. When Hirka turns 15, she is considered a grown woman who has to go through a certain ritual; the only problem is that because Hirka is </span>
  <span id="freeText577555361345773087" style="display:none">This is a YA fantasy story based on Norse Mythology. It was written by a Norwegian author, and so far it has only been published in Scandinavia, to my knowledge. <br />That being said, I definitely recommend this book if you are able to get it and read it. It tells the story of Hirka who is very different from everyone else around her - that's because she has no tail. When Hirka turns 15, she is considered a grown woman who has to go through a certain ritual; the only problem is that because Hirka is different, she's not sure she can complete that ritual like everyone else. The story takes off from there and becomes a long journey for both Hirka and her best friend Rime. <br />I really liked this novel because it became kind of nostalgic to me. It reminded me of when I was younger and enjoyed reading a fantasy novel now and again. Furthermore, this is a solid story that is not really predictable and that takes you on quite a fantastic journey. I didn't expect much from it, but I was definitely happy about it and enjoyed reading it from beginning to end. <br /><br />This is the first installment of a trilogy, in which the rest of the books will be out in Fall 2016 and Spring 2017. </span>
  <a data-text-id="577555361345773087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_748199072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/748199072" />
    <a title="Jan-egil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20739706-jan-egil"><img alt="Jan-egil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369641744p2/20739706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/748199072?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan-egil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan-egil" href="/user/show/20739706-jan-egil">Jan-egil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer748199072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1141234242362377050">Since this book is only in norwegian, I'm going to write this in norwegian. I really hope they will translate the book to english, because it's so good! I pity those who will not be able to read it because you don't understand the language. It's one of the best fantasybooks I've read in a long time, and it's a flavore of fantasy that's not easy to categorize. So since I don't know how long you will have to wait for the english version, you better start learning norwegian so that you won't miss i</span>
  <span id="freeText1141234242362377050" style="display:none">Since this book is only in norwegian, I'm going to write this in norwegian. I really hope they will translate the book to english, because it's so good! I pity those who will not be able to read it because you don't understand the language. It's one of the best fantasybooks I've read in a long time, and it's a flavore of fantasy that's not easy to categorize. So since I don't know how long you will have to wait for the english version, you better start learning norwegian so that you won't miss it!<br /><br />Odinsbarn er ingen lett bok å starte på, forfatteren går ikke ut i fra at leseren er en idiot og må holdes i hånden hele veien. Det er nok kanskje en "elsk-hat"-bok, enten får man ikke nok eller så faller man tidlig av. Jeg er i den første gruppen! Du blir sluppet rett inn i en verden du ikke kjenner, med uttrykk du ikke vet hva betyr. Gradvis lærer du verdenen å kjenne, og det er en fantastisk verden. En verden inspirert av gammel norrøn mytologi, men absolutt sin egen verden.<br /><br />Hovedpersonen Hirka er ei tøff jente, en som ikke passer inn noe sted, men likevel ikke lar seg kue. Persongalleriet er godt utviklet, selv de man føler kan være litt flate til å begynne med utvikler seg godt gjennom boken.<br /><br />Jeg vil anbefale denne boken for alle som liker "tradisjonell" fantasy, med en twist. Jeg sliter litt med å kategorisere den, den passer ikke godt inn i noen av undersjangrene til fantasy. Men du bør lese den. <br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2264748635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2264748635" />
    <a title="Lada" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22217810-lada"><img alt="Lada" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443475879p2/22217810.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2264748635?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lada" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lada" href="/user/show/22217810-lada">Lada</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788074915567" href="/book/show/29063391-dinovo-d-t">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2264748635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10577243361494330194">Rating this book is hard. I read it in czech, and I am sure something got lost in the translation, because I HATED, really really hated the way this book was written. <br/>I loved the world, but not how needlessly detailed everything was. I loved the concept I guess. But not the characters. Not a single one(or maybe Kuro?), and that was probably what made it so hard for me to read it. The pacing as well was so... slugish. I was bored most of the time. The book could be shorter. From the page 500 up, </span>
  <span id="freeText10577243361494330194" style="display:none">Rating this book is hard. I read it in czech, and I am sure something got lost in the translation, because I HATED, really really hated the way this book was written. <br />I loved the world, but not how needlessly detailed everything was. I loved the concept I guess. But not the characters. Not a single one(or maybe Kuro?), and that was probably what made it so hard for me to read it. The pacing as well was so... slugish. I was bored most of the time. The book could be shorter. From the page 500 up, I liked the action a lot. Ending not so much. Sentences were too short, clipped (my head spinned). I would prefer some of them merging into a longer one. I hated how characters knew what other persons thought just by looking at them. They(the author) didn't let me choose what to think of their actions. It felt manipulative sometimes.<br /><br />Yeah so, spoilers:<br />- first, I was thrown into this unknown world right away and I was annoyed for at least 50 pages, because nothing was explained to me, absolutely nothing. Characters just went on, but I was so confused (I just really hate these types of books. I don't want infodumps either, but would a little help in this mess hurt anybody?)<br />- the cover is so ugly and revolting<br /><br />Hirka<br />- I just don't like her. For one, I am tired of ginger protagonists. But I couldn't identify myself with her at all. She is 15 and acts stupid a lot. Yet sometimes, she acts as if she knows everything (so wise) or she is staring people down her nose while being one of them(of course she needs special treatment and she is not like others... it was towards the end, when the heigher-ups showed up at that Kolkagga hideout). She simply seems irrational to me. Why freeing that puppet man? She didn't know him at all!<br />- yeah, it's interesting how everybody loves her... I mean: her father, that dude that listents to the stone, Eirik, Tein, Rime of course, the man that leads the Kolkagga, that dude that sweared on his name that will protect and follow Rime, the man who owns the tea shop, Ramoja, Vetle... Basically every important man in an important possition huh? <br />- yet Hirka is so jealous of every girl! She is a tomboy and has no friends. Oh wait, she had one. But her friend from the village turned out to be a slut(of course), throwing herself at Rime, so that was that. And everytime Rime is near some other girl, Hirka goes like this: oh he can't love me, he can't have me because he would die and he will forget me in a few days and founds another...<br />- like.... girl, have some confidence in yourself. She kept belittling herself everytime, saying something like: Rime Al-blablabla, the heir, the blessed and feared, he is so above me I can't reach him, I can't dirt him with my hands, oh my what do I do... I just got tired of it quickly. She thinks he is a god and... just no<br />- they kissed (not once), acted so obvious... yet how can Hirka even think Rime doesn't know she likes him? And why can't she believe he likes her, dammit?! For the angst??<br />- her talk about plants and herbs was tiresome. I got that she didn't have much of a personality besides: I am a healer, I never saw violence, I will never let Rime win over me, I want to touch Rime, honeybread, climbing and being without a tail<br />- oh yeah... so they live in this medieval society right? Yet Hirka is so stunned to see violence? An actual fight with weapons and I am just like... why are you so surprised?<br />- Hirka thinks about Rime a lot. I began to cringe everytime Rime showed up in her thoughts. Her world is revolving around him, she thinks he is holy or something, she was willing to die for him (not once) and what was most hideous: that moment when Rime told her she is good and not mold/rot/blight (I don't know the translation for this one) and every worry of hers just melted away... NO, just no. A person doesn't need another person (a boy) to told them what they are to become confident... It just didn't felt right.<br />- so yeah, Hirka is stupid and I don't like her. She should have slept with Rime when she could, instead of creepily watching him naked by the pond or always staring at him with dripping saliva from her open mouth and dreaming about touching him, or him filling her (with a Force/Might, of course)<br />- what the hell was that scene where she went almost hysteric about her backpack? the hell<br />- also, when you are in a cave, at night, with a thunderstorm raging outside and no fire/light... you will probably not be able to see paleness of someone's lips, crescents under someone's eyes or their facial expressions, no? ... just sayin<br />- was that part with a tea shop necessary? why was that man even important? what a filler<br />- everything came to Hirka (in Ravnhov, in Manfalla), I didn't get a feeling she had it that hard. Rime always showed up in time to save her anyway<br /><br />Rime<br />- this boy is so melodramatic and emo, oh my<br />- he is always whinning how bad the life was to him... by him being rich, and from a respected family, with a brilliant future awaiting him<br />- but he is moping around instead of doing something with it, and then he rejects it all, just to show them who is in control (or something)<br />- also, Rime is beyong handsome, beyond skilled in martial arts and his enemies are shaking in fear when he enters the room<br />- also, he is just a young boy <br />- I don't know, maybe wolfs in this world have silver eyes. But it seems stupid to me to call his eyes "wolf's" when I imagine yellow or orange... IDK, it just felt wierd to me<br />- I found him too perfect (yet too whinny) to be likable<br />- why Rime and Hirka are supossed to love each other so much? They obssess over each other, yet they don't have any other friends. IDK. Everything is about these two and I DON'T FEEL IT<br /><br />- RAPE... in this book surprised me. There was no warning at the jacket. I was so repulsed to know Urd raped Ramoja (why going this way, dear author?), and ever more repulsed by that scene in dungeons. Was is necessary? Like, was it, really? Because how convinient, that someone showed up seconds before the man raped Hirka. Really, a lucky girl. Yet she doesn't suffer afterwards, and not 24h after, she wants to fuck Rime. So, why the hell was that in this book? Why?<br /><br />Urd. <br />- he could have been a better villian. He was impulsive and abusive and used violence often. Pfft. I was more scared when he was manipulating people, when he used his mind as a weapon. <br /><br />- I liked Kuro a lot<br /><br />- The rest of the characters.... nah. They did nothing to me. Too many names. Everybody seems to always like Hirka, because she always says what they need to hear. How convenient. I thought Tein will have a bigger role (wtf was that bathing scene with him and Hirka?? Again, what was the point?)<br /><br />- I liked everything about the Force/Might, it was so interesting. But here I am, having read entire book one, and I know not much about it. Nobody cared to explain how it works exactly, nobody commented on Hirka and her strange powers etc. <br />- the worldbulding... on one hand, the world is rich and interesting, but there were times when the tiniest details were described without being relevant<br />- Rime could appear changed towards the end, but he seems self-centered and selfish as always<br />- Hirka didn't change at all. No character development.<br />- Overall I am hopeful for the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10577243361494330194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1914109956" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1914109956" />
    <a title="Linda (un)Conventional Bookworms" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3651677-linda-un-conventional-bookworms"><img alt="Linda (un)Conventional Bookworms" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579882797p2/3651677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1914109956?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda (un)Conventional Bookworms" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda (un)Conventional Bookworms" href="/user/show/3651677-linda-un-conventional-bookworms">Linda (un)Conventional Bookworms</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788205467095" href="/book/show/24581229-odinsbarn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3651677-linda-un-conventional-bookworms?shelf=original-language">original-language</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3651677-linda-un-conventional-bookworms?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3651677-linda-un-conventional-bookworms?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3651677-linda-un-conventional-bookworms?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3651677-linda-un-conventional-bookworms?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3651677-linda-un-conventional-bookworms?shelf=norwegian-author">norwegian-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3651677-linda-un-conventional-bookworms?shelf=2017-fave-reads">2017-fave-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1914109956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6689334905596874176"><b>
  <a href='https://unconventionalbookviews.com/review-odinsbarn-siri-pettersen/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>This review was originally posted on (un)Conventional Bookviews</a>
</b><br/>Odinsbarn is a fantasy that includes the kind of epic-ness that is so hard to find it seems almost impossible. Alas, it's completely possible!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452078466i/17642323.jpg' alt='Review - (un)Conventional Bookviews' width='300' height='80' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Odinsbarn is a fantastic story, where the mythology has a certain Norse feel to it. Where the 12-person council that rules over the world seems to be rotten on the inside; all the while fearing the rot of those that are other. I found the fear of other and how that fear was dealt with to be</span>
  <span id="freeText6689334905596874176" style="display:none"><b>
  <a href="https://unconventionalbookviews.com/review-odinsbarn-siri-pettersen/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was originally posted on (un)Conventional Bookviews</a>
</b><br>Odinsbarn is a fantasy that includes the kind of epic-ness that is so hard to find it seems almost impossible. Alas, it's completely possible!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452078466i/17642323.jpg" alt="Review - (un)Conventional Bookviews" width="300" height="80" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Odinsbarn is a fantastic story, where the mythology has a certain Norse feel to it. Where the 12-person council that rules over the world seems to be rotten on the inside; all the while fearing the rot of those that are other. I found the fear of other and how that fear was dealt with to be both fascinating and accurate. The folks in this story were proud of their tails, their history, and their ability to share energy with the earth.The Seer was there to protect them from the blind, and I was so completely immersed in the story from beginning to end it was difficult to put the book down to get some sleep.<br><br>Hirka is definitely other, she is the tail-less, possibly an Odinchild, and she is both feared and looked at with disgust.<br>The world building is amazing, and I can't say it enough, this has to be translated to English so all my English-speaking friends can get immersed with the ravens, the ability, the all-aroundness, and the fight for justice. The writing is so well done, though, so the translator would have to be able to also transform some of the wordplay in order for the whole story to have the same voice and feel to it as in the original version.<br><br>Odinsbarn is both plot and character driven, with Hirka a fantastic heroine. She is young, and in some instances, I felt that. In other instances, though, she was able to see much farther than herself and her close circle to understand things much older characters didn't even begin to grasp. Her inner strength was both calm and sure, and when she was afraid of something, she embraced that fear and made it her own. Dealing with it, feeling it and the she could move forward once more.<br><br>Odinsbarn is tight, and it is solidly built on the foundations of Norse mythology. The author managed to use the mythology as a building block and then make it her own, though. And of course, I will go straight to the next book - Råta (The Rot) - so I can see if any of my predictions turn out to be true. Because the fact that these folks are afraid of humns, and they think Hirka is an Odinchild. They use ravens both for protection and as a guid makes me think there is still much more to both the story and the world(s) than what conclusions I have made so far.<br><br>Written in third person point of view, past tense, and mostly from Hirka's perspective, Odinsbarn grabbed my interest in a different way than any YA fantasy has done. Maybe because of the Norse roots? Maybe because the very distinct voice of Hirka? Maybe because the times when I got parts of the story from a different character's perspective it truly brought something both interesting and vital to the story? I can't really explain it, but if you enjoy YA fantasy, you should cross your fingers and your toes for a translation. Not sure if there are any ears we can try to whisper to?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452078466i/17642324.jpg" alt="Fave Quotes - (un)Conventional Bookviews" width="300" height="80" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><em>Rime warned of danger, she felt it in every single one of her nerves. She had thought she'd recognized him, but what she saw in front of her was only a memory. The man in front of her was no childhood rival.</em><br><br><em>Father looked at her. His eyes were deep and withered like his legs. This was how it was going to be. She was a wrongborn who couldn't share the energy. She was blind for the Ability. Cheated of what everyone else had. Ability-less. And tail-less. </em><br><br><em>The room smelled like leather from the bindings. And power. It smelled like power. This was how power was supposed to smell. Everlasting. Immortal. Boundless.</em><br><br><em>She closed her eyes against his chest and listened to the beats of his heart. The best sound she'd ever heard. The best she'd ever felt. And also the worst. She had tasted something that could never be hers. Not without killing him. It was too much to bear.</em><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6689334905596874176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2063408094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2063408094" />
    <a title="Joanka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20233424-joanka"><img alt="Joanka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476184344p2/20233424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2063408094?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanka" href="/user/show/20233424-joanka">Joanka</a>
      </span>

          marked it as abandoned




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=fantasy-scifi-and-co">fantasy-scifi-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=women">women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=europe">europe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=scandinavia-nordics-and-co">scandinavia-nordics-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2063408094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16170895380040522254">DNF around 100 page.<br/><br/>So! There is this book marketed as something amazingly original, a new wave of fantasy, SCANDINAVIAN fantasy! How original it is, to have Scandinavian folklore and mythology-based world in fantasy?! (Um, wait.)<br/><br/>To do the book justice, the world is described pretty nice and it felt consistent. Of course, there is the curiosity of creating a new race that is… human beings with tails. That’s it. Oh, of course they have magic, but we are talking about a fantasy world, I guess ever</span>
  <span id="freeText16170895380040522254" style="display:none">DNF around 100 page.<br /><br />So! There is this book marketed as something amazingly original, a new wave of fantasy, SCANDINAVIAN fantasy! How original it is, to have Scandinavian folklore and mythology-based world in fantasy?! (Um, wait.)<br /><br />To do the book justice, the world is described pretty nice and it felt consistent. Of course, there is the curiosity of creating a new race that is… human beings with tails. That’s it. Oh, of course they have magic, but we are talking about a fantasy world, I guess everyone suspected that. Also, the map doesn’t make sense to me in reference to the text of the book.<br /><br />Enter our fifteen years old heroine. The originality continues! Hirka is a feisty redhead, not like the other girls and generally not like the other aetlings – she has no tail and she can’t use magic. There is a special coming-of-age ritual on the horizon, that determines your place in the world, on the basis of how well you deal with magic. Hirka is not excited about it but then she learns that she should be scared – she is not a tailless aetling but a creature of different race and that a man she called father found her on a winter night in a circle of magical stones! The race she seems to come from is believed to be legends but also is feared and Hirka must run away to save her life! Enter the hero, three years older noble boy who resign from titles to be a soldier and has a mission so secret he can’t even mention it in his thoughts during his POV! Of course Hirka used to be his only friend because she never paid attention to his titles but did all sorts of risky and fun stuff with him. Enter the antagonist, another teenage boy, who this time was willing to do everything to get titles and become a part of a special Council. He is not even shying away from allying with dark forces! Or killing his father! Does he eat mice while off-screen?!<br /><br />Then of course everything blows up. Did you REALLY think Hirka has no powers?! Ha!<br /><br />So, if that speaks to you, you should try Pettersen novel. The style is not painful and many people describe it as flowing, I’m not that sure, for me it was too chopped and everything is explained twice so that you understand it for sure, dear reader.<br /><br />Not my cup of tea, maybe it becomes better later but I have no time to risk reading the whole trilogy while I don’t enjoy it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16170895380040522254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer767379222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13775165499169467957">HOLY CRAP I feel so sorry for all who can't read Norwegian because HOLY HELL this is a quality book which has everything!!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer17891349938330298114">Full review at <a href='http://bookishloveaffair.blogspot.dk/2017/07/odinsbarn-ravneringene-1-af-siri.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookish Love Affair</a>.<br/><br/>What a wonderful piece of fantasy litterature. With its roots in an aspect of Norse Mythology that seems kind of unknown and overlooked to me, we follow Hirka on a gripping journey as she tries to come to terms with the startling reveal of what she is. She's always been different, she has no tail. And it wasn't a wolf that took it. She's never had it, because she is a <i>odinsbarn</i> (litteraly "child of Odin"), a creature feared and mythical in the world where she l</span>
  <span id="freeText17891349938330298114" style="display:none">Full review at <a href="http://bookishloveaffair.blogspot.dk/2017/07/odinsbarn-ravneringene-1-af-siri.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookish Love Affair</a>.<br /><br />What a wonderful piece of fantasy litterature. With its roots in an aspect of Norse Mythology that seems kind of unknown and overlooked to me, we follow Hirka on a gripping journey as she tries to come to terms with the startling reveal of what she is. She's always been different, she has no tail. And it wasn't a wolf that took it. She's never had it, because she is a <i>odinsbarn</i> (litteraly "child of Odin"), a creature feared and mythical in the world where she lives. How did she get there?<br /><br />But what's more important is how does she stay alive, if word gets out, shes's a good as dead. But Hirka is a wonderful main character and although she first flees to save her own life, she turns who she is into a way of trying to help, when it radually becomes clear that the ruling group of people is more than a little corrupt. There's magic, strange creatures, betrayal, friendship and a little romance, but underneath it all is a damn good story written in the most beautiful language. So far, this book has only come out in Scandinavia as far as I know, but I hope it'll get published in English. Because it is quite simply good.</span>

<div id="review_2110907575" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2110907575" />
    <a title="marlene " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013434-marlene"><img alt="marlene " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536372997p2/4013434.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2110907575?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="marlene " class="user" itemprop="url" name="marlene " href="/user/show/4013434-marlene">marlene </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013434-marlene?shelf=top-favorites">top-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013434-marlene?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2110907575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3645303682330453110"><b>You know when you've had this book sitting on your shelf forever and then you finally read it and want to punch yourself in your face for not reading it sooner!?</b><br/><br/><u>
  <i>Odinsbarn by Siri Pettersen: </i>
</u><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Imagine missing something everyone else has,<br/>something that proves you belong to this world.<br/>Something so vital, that without it, you're nobody.<br/>A plague. A myth. A human."</i>
</b><br/><i><br/>Fifteen winters old, Hirka learns that she is an Odin's child – a tailless rot from another world. Despised. Dreaded. And hunted. Sh</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3645303682330453110" style="display:none"><b>You know when you've had this book sitting on your shelf forever and then you finally read it and want to punch yourself in your face for not reading it sooner!?</b><br /><br /><u>
  <i>Odinsbarn by Siri Pettersen: </i>
</u><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Imagine missing something everyone else has,<br />something that proves you belong to this world.<br />Something so vital, that without it, you're nobody.<br />A plague. A myth. A human."</i>
</b><br /><i><br />Fifteen winters old, Hirka learns that she is an Odin's child – a tailless rot from another world. Despised. Dreaded. And hunted. She no longer knows who she is, and someone wants to kill her to keep it a secret. But there are worse things than humans, and Hirka is not the only creature to have broken through the gates…<br /><br />"In THE RAVEN RINGS series the classic elements of fantasy literature have been reinvented. There are no prophecies, no dragons, and no magic swords. There is magic, to be sure, but you won't find that word in the book. The protagonist is a resourceful, female outcast, living with a savage Northerner who deals drugs. She is not "chosen", and has no special powers. In fact, what sets her apart is the terrifying fact that she lacks the powers that everyone else has.<br /><br />The series has been maturing in the head of the author for almost a decade. Dealing with matters of xenophobia, blind faith and the right or will to lead, this is epic fantasy literature with a purpose."</i><br />- from ravenrings.com.<br /><br />Odinsbarn (which I guess translates to "odinschild") actually is the first book I've read in Norwegian for probably 10+ years. Honestly the fact that it was a Norwegian book was part of the reason I never got around to reading it. Over the years I got in the habit of reading english and never had any Norwegian books really grab my attention enough for me to go out and buy it. But last year I wanted to give Norwegian authors a chance and the first book I bought was Odinsbarn. I knew it to be one of the most popular fantasy books here. Still, it took me ages to start it! I've had a horrible reading year so far - I've just been distracted by life. I almost never took the time to read and the book had to be pretty damn amazing to keep my attention for more than 15 minutes.. <br /><br />Well, now I've been dragging this 600+ page book around with me for a week. I've been reading on the bus to/from school, at school during breaks, on fishing trips and of course curled up on the couch and even better - outside on our balcony. This book is best read outside, breathing the fresh air. You'll know if you read it. <br /><br />I really don't know how to describe this book and write a decent review. I'm sad I can't find the words to explain in a "short" review because I don't think this book has been translated to english yet (WHY?) and I want you all to be able to read it. I truly think so many of you would love it!<br />There was a few things that I wish were different (I'm very critical about relationships in particular) but nothing that would keep me from giving this book a million stars if I could. The plot is so unlike anythings I've ever read. This was the best reading experience I've had in a long time. I hope this book will be translated to english soon so more of you guys can experience this world too.<br /><br />I'm definitely diving right into the next book in the Raven Rings trilogy to see what Hirka and Rime will get up to. I have "Råta" right next to me right now, I had to run and get it off my shelf as soon as I finished Odinsbarn - that ending was epic! Kind of happy I'm late to read this trilogy, the wait for the next book would have been painful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3645303682330453110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1915277407" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1915277407" />
    <a title="Caroline Stan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44426890-caroline-stan"><img alt="Caroline Stan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590338717p2/44426890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1915277407?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline Stan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline Stan" href="/user/show/44426890-caroline-stan">Caroline Stan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<div id="review_2043356404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2043356404" />
    <a title="Fipah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39755297-fipah"><img alt="Fipah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567364344p2/39755297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2043356404?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fipah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fipah" href="/user/show/39755297-fipah">Fipah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788074915567" href="/book/show/29063391-dinovo-d-t">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39755297-fipah?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2043356404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7342444583114483763"><b> 1 star = I did not like it. </b><br/><br/><i>First of all let me say I am not a fan of cold hardcore Medival-ish fantasy, and I do not read books similar to this one. I perfer warm-hearted fantasy in the style of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/769483.Magyk__Septimus_Heap___1_' title='Magyk (Septimus Heap, #1) by Angie Sage' rel='nofollow noopener'>Magyk</a> or the ineffable <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18116.His_Dark_Materials__His_Dark_Materials__1_3_' title='His Dark Materials (His Dark Materials #1-3) by Philip Pullman' rel='nofollow noopener'>His Dark Materials</a>, so my review may be skewed. I quit reading after having read 473 pages out of 559. I tried to read it because of the amazing reviews. </i><br/><br/>Personally, I found it very hard to <b> imagine </b> any concept or place in this book - the author revels in indirect hints that ser</span>
  <span id="freeText7342444583114483763" style="display:none"><b> 1 star = I did not like it. </b><br /><br /><i>First of all let me say I am not a fan of cold hardcore Medival-ish fantasy, and I do not read books similar to this one. I perfer warm-hearted fantasy in the style of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/769483.Magyk__Septimus_Heap___1_" title="Magyk (Septimus Heap, #1) by Angie Sage" rel="nofollow noopener">Magyk</a> or the ineffable <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18116.His_Dark_Materials__His_Dark_Materials__1_3_" title="His Dark Materials (His Dark Materials #1-3) by Philip Pullman" rel="nofollow noopener">His Dark Materials</a>, so my review may be skewed. I quit reading after having read 473 pages out of 559. I tried to read it because of the amazing reviews. </i><br /><br />Personally, I found it very hard to <b> imagine </b> any concept or place in this book - the author revels in indirect hints that serve as a complete foundation of the world building. Throughout the book we are introduced to various practices that indeed are named, yet remain vague and grey only to be slowly unraveled over the course of several hundred pages. The world remains uninteresting, brute and to me it felt there was nothing that enriched me throughout the reading process - I did not care about the world, the plot, nor its characters.<br /><br /><b>I feel like the reader is required to "get" it, yet there is so little offered.</b> Even with descriptions I found I could not imagine the world - say a room or a building was described, but anything specific was omitted - should I imagine it as something resembling typical medieval fantasy and its setting or does it look more alien? Traditional? Northern? Is it flashy purple?<br />The reader is just thrown into the world, which sometimes can be a good thing - here it was not.<br />I could never taste the world, breathe in its winds.<br /><br />The author's constant third-person thoughts that are meant to make the plot complex are clichéd, and in my opinion they do not serve the plot. On the contrary, it feels as if Ms Pettersen wants to say what we should be thinking about the plot in the voice of the characters. The thoughts are much richer than the dialogue itself, but this leaves us with a poor dialogue filled with variegated shards of thought that are meant to elevate its complexity. Though being poorly written, one can not elevate it anywhere - it needs to be rewritten. It goes something like this: <br /><br /><i>Fact A happens in a dialogue.<br />Character B explains what happened and the implications of it with their thoughts.<br />Character B replies.<br />Now we see character C's thoughts on the situation.<br />Character C retaliates with a phrase said in a valorous manner.<br />Then we are offered a view what this really means to this character.<br />Character B lets it sink in.<br />Character B replies.</i><br /><br /><b>With all the unnaturalness and clunkiness of the dialogues aside, I think it was also confusing how the points of view (POV) switched - I think they were executed poorly. </b> It was hard to follow the often clunky changes from limited third person POV to the involved (aka omniscient) author POV to the observer-narrator (3rd person) POV. Here I use the POV names as explained by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/874602.Ursula_K__Le_Guin" title="Ursula K. Le Guin" rel="nofollow noopener">Ursula K. Le Guin</a> in her excellent <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68024.Steering_the_Craft_Exercises_and_Discussions_on_Story_Writing_for_the_Lone_Navigator_or_the_Mutinous_Crew" title="Steering the Craft Exercises and Discussions on Story Writing for the Lone Navigator or the Mutinous Crew by Ursula K. Le Guin" rel="nofollow noopener">Steering the Craft: Exercises and Discussions on Story Writing for the Lone Navigator or the Mutinous Crew</a>. This left me feeling detached from both the dialogue and the story, unsure whom it actually was telling me the story. <br /><br />Last but not least, the conflict is hard to empathise with and in the book it is presented after approximately 300 pages; up until then it feels like a blind and unenjoyable walk full of trite dialogues wherein the characters speak in a stilted heroic manner that feels unnatural. <br /><br /><b>tl;dr: Not recommended if medieval/cold North-style fantasy is not your style, especially when the world's omnipresent culture and customs are left unexplained while forming the basis of the conflict - think an individual VS society and its collective fault. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7342444583114483763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2006925980" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2006925980" />
    <a title="Ell Eastwood" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31527173-ell-eastwood"><img alt="Ell Eastwood" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400523261p2/31527173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2006925980?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ell Eastwood" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ell Eastwood" href="/user/show/31527173-ell-eastwood">Ell Eastwood</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789132164859" href="/book/show/24807756-odinsbarn">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31527173-ell-eastwood?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31527173-ell-eastwood?shelf=read-in-swedish">read-in-swedish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31527173-ell-eastwood?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31527173-ell-eastwood?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31527173-ell-eastwood?shelf=tw-rape">tw-rape</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2006925980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9247462391610553577">Does this book live up to the hype? No. I will go as far as to say that it has been overhyped and is not nearly as good as everyone says. It's like in Unbreakable Kimmy Schmidt when Mikey says Cate Blanchett is a great actress and Titus responds "is she? Or is she just tall?". Is this book good or is it just long? Spoiler: it's just long.<br/><br/>Honestly, I'm not saying all books that are this long are bad, but unless it's like idk Stephen King's IT or Lord of the Rings, there probably could have been s</span>
  <span id="freeText9247462391610553577" style="display:none">Does this book live up to the hype? No. I will go as far as to say that it has been overhyped and is not nearly as good as everyone says. It's like in Unbreakable Kimmy Schmidt when Mikey says Cate Blanchett is a great actress and Titus responds "is she? Or is she just tall?". Is this book good or is it just long? Spoiler: it's just long.<br /><br />Honestly, I'm not saying all books that are this long are bad, but unless it's like idk Stephen King's IT or Lord of the Rings, there probably could have been some cuts and edits. So is the case here. At first I had gotten the idea that the author was very young and was like "I'll cut her some slack", but that wasn't really the case so now there's not really any excuses. Don't let a debut author write 600 pages unedited.<br /><br />And it feels very unedited to me? The writing is rambly, constantly going over the same things again and again and again, and sometimes concepts are introduced at a part of the story where they should have been mentioned already. It feels like the author just kept writing thinking "I'll fix that in editing" and never did (though I'm sure the book was edited, it just doesn't feel that way).<br /><br />Plus it just does a lot of things that bothers me in writing. Cursive thoughts that have already been explained in plain text. Waaaaaay more exclamation marks than are necessary. Witty dialogue that honestly just made me cringe. And it can't really decide on whether it should use a modern language or more archaic and settles for a mix that just doesn't work.<br /><br />All these things made it very had for me to relate to the protagonists, who aren't very interesting people. Hirka is ????. She's like your typical YA protagonist in that she doesn't have much of a personality and just changes it whenever the scene needs her to. She's a bit egocentric and very convinced the world is out to get her, which is often true but not always. Her love interest, Rime, is like every Edward Cullen tragic-angsty-broody dude you've seen. And as in Twilight there's of course reasons they can never kiss or have sex that are ... kinda problematic. Because shaming girls, even for magical reasons, for having sex or wanting sex is kinda last century.<br /><br />Plus I think the ball was dropped with the world-building. It takes way too long for tails to be mentioned given the premise of the book and they don't seem to play a particularly big part in Hirkas life? Which seems weird to me because I feel tails should be a big part of the body language of the world, but it's not. I never get the sense that Hirka is having trouble expressing herself for her lack of tail or that any of the other characters give themselves away by a tail twitch they didn't intend to do. It feels like a missed opportunity.<br /><br />So why three stars? Idk, maybe because I liked the basis in norse mythology or because it was nice to be reading proper high fantasy again, where people hang at inns and throw beer at each other. It's not something I read that much these days and it made me nostalgic. And given the end of the book I am, annoyingly enough, interested in how it continues.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9247462391610553577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_875549330" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/875549330" />
    <a title="L." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2033651-l"><img alt="L." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1236435975p2/2033651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/875549330?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L." class="user" itemprop="url" name="L." href="/user/show/2033651-l">L.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2033651-l?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2033651-l?shelf=norwegian">norwegian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2033651-l?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer875549330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12391510005991759380">I debated a bit with myself whether to give this book four or five stars because as much as I liked it, there were a few moments where I kind of lost interest a little bit. I also thought that while the language was good, there were a lot of places where I thought it would have made sense to start a new paragraph, only that didn't happen and that made the book feel rushed in places where it would have been nice to get a moment to breathe. <br/><br/>But I decided that those things are just details, really.</span>
  <span id="freeText12391510005991759380" style="display:none">I debated a bit with myself whether to give this book four or five stars because as much as I liked it, there were a few moments where I kind of lost interest a little bit. I also thought that while the language was good, there were a lot of places where I thought it would have made sense to start a new paragraph, only that didn't happen and that made the book feel rushed in places where it would have been nice to get a moment to breathe. <br /><br />But I decided that those things are just details, really. It's nothing in the big picture. Because all in all I thought this was a really great book. The universe is amazingly built and the characters are interesting. The book is also something new, something I've never read before. I like fantasy, but sometimes the stories can be too similar. This book doesn't remind me of anything I've read before, and that's one of the best things about it.<br /><br />The book also blew all the skepticism I might have had about Norwegian fantasy right out the window. I thought it might be too simple and not as deep and complex as I wanted it to be, but I had no reason to worry. This is a really good book, an amazing universe, and I can't wait for the next book to be released so I can find out what happens next!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12391510005991759380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11404003675328458720" style="display:none">Heart.<br /><br />I read this because my friend gave it to me for christmas, and she insisted I had to at least try. I'm an idiot when it comes to reading new books (and watching new films), so I was more interested in re-reading the Harry Potter books while re-listening to my Harry Potter audiobooks and re-watching the Harry Potter films. I mean, my sister got me the set of books that creates Hogwarts with the backs, and of course that makes it a top priority even though I've read and heard the books in both English and Norwegian 3-4 times, right. But I gave in and started. And holy moly, I've almost eaten the book (I think you can see a bitemark). <br /><br />I'm not a good book reviewer, so I can't really say anything smart about how well it's written and how deep the story and content is, but I absolutely loved it. The only thing I didn't love was the fact that it ended. Suddenly there were no pages left and I had a lil meltdown when I realized I didn't have the second book. So I ordered it 2:30 in the morning and lived in the mailbox waiting for it to arrive. <br /><br />Now I have Odinsbarn and Råta in paperback, so I can't get Evna yet, because it's only available in hard case and my inner OCD is even more idiot than I am. <br /><br />But hello, read this book.</span>

    <a title="Isabel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17355900-isabel"><img alt="Isabel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561124069p2/17355900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1795212861?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isabel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isabel" href="/user/show/17355900-isabel">Isabel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1795212861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer749954501855979935">I heard on the audiobook for this for just an hour while I was cleaning and I read the rest. But I have to commend the male narrator, he has a beautiful voice and I really enjoyed it. It's just in Norwegian, so that's awful I guess. I love how the author has borrowed from Norse mythology - you can see it in the world building and everywhere around Hirka and Siri Petterson has created something for me which is magic. The book is pretty long in my opinion - but everything feels like it needs to be</span>
  <span id="freeText749954501855979935" style="display:none">I heard on the audiobook for this for just an hour while I was cleaning and I read the rest. But I have to commend the male narrator, he has a beautiful voice and I really enjoyed it. It's just in Norwegian, so that's awful I guess. I love how the author has borrowed from Norse mythology - you can see it in the world building and everywhere around Hirka and Siri Petterson has created something for me which is magic. The book is pretty long in my opinion - but everything feels like it needs to be there. It makes sense. It adds to the world, our Hirka or what is happening to her. <br /><br />I love Hirka's character, and her insecurities. I love how she is portrayed and her relationship to herself. Hirka doesn't have a tail. Yep, you read that right. And people who don't got a tail are crazy, or "odinsbarn" which has got "råta" (holy shit trying to explain this shit in English is fucking cray) -and I'm getting ahead of myself but Hirka has believed her whole life that her tail got taken by a wolf when she was a small child. Which is not the case. <br /><br />The relationship between Hirka and Rime is beautiful. Well, I do think its beautiful. I think the bond between Hirka and her father is magnificent and I loved reading about it. About how they were essentially living on the edge in this world, and Hirkas relation to it all. <br /><br />I love this book - and I would highly recommend it to other people out there. (English version soon pls)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17579058642656338727">A great book that was gifted to me by my friend Lene, so that didn't have any idea what was awaiting me!     <a title="Selina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71352871-selina"><img alt="Selina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604947551p2/71352871.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2477282727?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Selina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Selina" href="/user/show/71352871-selina">Selina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9783038801139" href="/book/show/40243305-odinskind">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71352871-selina?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2477282727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1602737926992142245">Although this book has a norse setting, norse mythology, norse names and a cool blurb, the rest of it - the writing, the telling and the characters - did not work for me.<br/>* The lack of clear information: The world is so detailed but still the important and basic things like how someone looks, who the Seer is, what the ritual is all about... is either mentioned accidentally or very late. I had to assume very much. Like, are the Yrms like humans just with a tail? And if the tail is the only differe</span>
  <span id="freeText1602737926992142245" style="display:none">Although this book has a norse setting, norse mythology, norse names and a cool blurb, the rest of it - the writing, the telling and the characters - did not work for me.<br />* The lack of clear information: The world is so detailed but still the important and basic things like how someone looks, who the Seer is, what the ritual is all about... is either mentioned accidentally or very late. I had to assume very much. Like, are the Yrms like humans just with a tail? And if the tail is the only difference, why are they mentioned rarely? It's like they are just an accessoire.<br />* The writing: This story is translated from norwegian, so I kept reading even when I found strange phrases. But still there was something about how the story was told that my reading flow was constantly interrupted. Especially when characters had a dialogue, they said something then they thought something and then I forgot what was said before and had to reread. For a 500 pages book I expect a fluid writing style.<br />* The most important thing: the characters. I did not like Hirka. On the one hand she's all tough and fearless but on the other hand she is a stupid teenager. She prouds herself of treating Rime like any other person but one second later she wails about how unreachable he is for her and that she is not worthy of him. The story goes on and on and it takes ages for things to get rolling.<br />I thought this book would be about an outsider girl who has to fight her way up, but Hirka? She's planless. She's running around a lot. I don't feel like the community hates her at all (except that one dumb bully). Hirka annoyed me very much, Rime didn't impress me either. Or Urd. The only one I really liked was Kuro the Raven.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1602737926992142245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12433203074696732841">I had to force myself, several times, to continue reading this book. <br/>Although in the end, I am now thinking that I have to read the next one, due to the cliffhanger ending. The language, in the Swedish version, is contrived and strained, with superfluous word use that just irritates. The story and premise could have been told with a less forced vocabulary in my opinion. I am not a writer at all, and I could not write a book. I have read a lot of books, and I certainly was underwhelmed and irrita</span>
  <span id="freeText12433203074696732841" style="display:none">I had to force myself, several times, to continue reading this book. <br />Although in the end, I am now thinking that I have to read the next one, due to the cliffhanger ending. The language, in the Swedish version, is contrived and strained, with superfluous word use that just irritates. The story and premise could have been told with a less forced vocabulary in my opinion. I am not a writer at all, and I could not write a book. I have read a lot of books, and I certainly was underwhelmed and irritated by the writing in this one. I want to emphasize that the story itself is good and I am interested to follow the characters in the series. Hopefully, I will not be as bothered by the next two books. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lrKp1C/eUUHnEkw3ABqoEBsFKrGO1JR+oAkvxGBW7L4oXbR9OfBU1cuYRseFvK2d9rdiByz/c6cdURfVoz8tNw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ru392SrMfd8Bmj0ZgsUVoiSgL+R6fgCKkhElbl50Ft4QAuBwPOJ4Sy0QN+kHYxAvyRJnUthV51MvSR1/nR3XVw==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3202417009437537523">Siri was born in 1971, under the northern lights of Norway, with a severely overactive imagination. It survived countless attacks from the outside world, rendering her an expert escapist, frolicking in a wide range of media: Design, web, comics, illustration, animation and text. Anything for a good story. In 2002 she won a national comic contest with "Anticlimax", the comic strip that made her "Ne</span>
  <span id="freeText3202417009437537523" style="display:none">Siri was born in 1971, under the northern lights of Norway, with a severely overactive imagination. It survived countless attacks from the outside world, rendering her an expert escapist, frolicking in a wide range of media: Design, web, comics, illustration, animation and text. Anything for a good story. In 2002 she won a national comic contest with "Anticlimax", the comic strip that made her "Newcomer of the year" in the Norwegian Sproing Awards. Siri has worked as an Art Director for many years, but she is now writing full time, devoted to her fantastical worlds.</span>
